67
That's so scary. But also-  You can make perfect hard-boiled eggs with a simple method that uses cold water and an ice bath to prevent overcooking and make them easy to peel.  Ingredients Eggs Cold water Ice Instructions Place eggs in a pot. Place the eggs in a single layer in a saucepan large enough to hold them without crowding. This helps them cook evenly. Cover with cold water. Add cold water until it covers the eggs by about one inch. Bring to a boil. Place the pot on high heat and bring the water to a full, rolling boil. Cover and remove from heat. As soon as the water reaches a boil, turn off the heat and cover the pot with a lid. Let the eggs stand. Let the eggs sit in the hot water. The standing time will depend on your preferred level of doneness. 9â€“12 minutes for large eggs. 10 minutes for creamy, vibrant yolks. 12 minutes for paler, firmer yolks. Reduce the time for medium eggs and increase it for extra-large eggs. Prepare an ice bath. While the eggs are cooking, fill a large bowl with ice water. Transfer eggs to the ice bath. When the time is up, use a slotted spoon to move the eggs from the hot water into the ice bath. This "shocks" the eggs and stops the cooking process. Cool completely. Let the eggs chill for at least five minutes in the ice bath. This makes them easier to peel. Peel and serve. Once cooled, tap the egg gently on a hard surface to crack the shell, then roll it between your hands to loosen it further. Peel under cool running water for the cleanest results.                                                                                             Oh and also. 67!!!
